============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO33)
============================================================
GT: -c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v - omega0**c3*(gamma*t + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidate formulas: 98

GT (fully expanded):
\[
-0.459914680311301\,v(1-v^2)\;-\;1.87329057400732\,v\;-\;2.49934616662645\,x(0.0579034145056311\,t+1)\;-\;2.49934616662645\,x
\]
Expand terms:
- Velocity part:
\[
-0.459914680311301\,v + 0.459914680311301\,v^3 - 1.87329057400732\,v
= 0.459914680311301\,v^3 - 2.333205254318621\,v
\]
- Position/time part:
\[
-2.49934616662645\,x(0.0579034145056311\,t+1) - 2.49934616662645\,x
= -(2.49934616662645\cdot 0.0579034145056311)\,t x - 4.9986923332529\,x
\]
Compute \(2.49934616662645\cdot 0.0579034145056311 \approx 0.144721\) (enough to identify structure).

So GT is exactly a polynomial of the form:
\[
(\text{const})\,v^3 + (\text{const})\,v + (\text{const})\,t x + (\text{const})\,x
\]
with **no** constants, no pure \(t\) term, no nonlinear-in-\(x\) terms, no trig/exp/log, and **no Abs/Max**.

Therefore, any candidate that can reduce (by setting some parameters to 0 and choosing exponents appropriately) to
\[
c_x x + c_v v + c_{v3} v^3 + c_{tx} t x
\]
can match, by picking those four coefficients equal to the GT’s four coefficients.

Below, for each candidate: I check whether it can be reduced to exactly \(\{x, v, v^3, tx\}\) only, with no extra unavoidable terms (including Abs).

---

### 1
Has extra \(\sin(\cdots)\) term. Can set \(c4=0\) to remove it → becomes \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 v^3 + c3 tx\). **Match possible.**

### 2
Has rational terms in \(t\). To remove them set \(c4=0\) and \(c7=0\) → same core polynomial. **Match possible.**

### 3
Contains constant \(c1\) (can set 0), \(x^{c3}\) (can set \(c2=0\)), and \(v\mathrm{Abs}(v)^2\) (this is \(v|v|^2\), not equal to \(v^3\) for negative \(v\); must set \(c4=0\)). Then left with \(c0x + c5 v + c6 t(c7+x)^{c8}\). That last term cannot become exactly \(tx\) without also introducing extra \(t\)-only pieces unless forced carefully; but you can set \(c6=0\) to remove it, leaving no \(tx\). So cannot get all four required terms simultaneously. **No match.**

### 4
Similar to 3; trig term removable by \(c6=0\), but then no \(tx\). Abs-term must be 0. **No match.**

### 5
Has \(x/(c1+x^2)\) term; must set \(c0=0\) to avoid non-polynomial. Also has constant \(c5\) (set 0) and \(t(c7+x)^{c8}\) (set \(c6=0\) or it won’t be linear \(tx\)). Then left \(c2 v + c3 v^3 + c4 x\) missing \(tx\). **No match.**

### 6
Has constant \(c0\) (set 0), exp term (set \(c1=0\)), \(x\cos(c6 t)\) (must set \(c5=0\) because cannot equal linear \(x\) and \(tx\) for all \(t\)), and \(t(c8+x)^{c9}\) (cannot be exactly \(tx\) without extra \(t\) unless you set it off). So can’t get exact GT. **No match.**

### 7
Has \(x/(c1+x^2)\) and \(x/(c7 t+c8)\) and \(1/(c7 t+c8)\); must zero those coefficients to avoid non-polynomial → then no \(tx\). **No match.**

### 8
Has \(\sin(c3 t+c4)\) removable by \(c2=0\). Then \(c0x+c1v+c5v^3+c6tx\). **Match possible.**

### 9
Has rational in \(x\): \(t/(c5 x+c6)\) and \(1/(c5 x+c6)\). Must set \(c4=c7=0\). Then core polynomial remains. **Match possible.**

### 10
Has rational in \(v\): removable by \(c4=c7=0\). Then core polynomial remains. **Match possible.**

### 11
Has extra \(c4 t + c5\). Must set \(c4=0,c5=0\). Then core polynomial remains. **Match possible.**

### 12
Has constant \(c1\) (set 0), Abs term \(v|v|^2\) (must set \(c2=0\)), and \(t(c5+x)^{c6}\) (cannot guarantee exactly \(tx\) without extra \(t\) unless special). If set \(c6=1\), term is \(c4 t(c5+x)=c4 c5 t + c4 tx\) introduces unwanted \(t\) unless \(c5=0\). Then it becomes \(c4 tx\). Great: with \(c6=1, c5=0\) we get \(c0x + c3 v + c4 tx\) but still missing \(v^3\). No \(v^3\) term exists. **No match.**

### 13
Has constant \(c1\) and pure \(t\) term \(c2 t\) (set both 0), Abs term (must set \(c3=0\)). Left \(c0x + c4 v + c5 tx\) missing \(v^3\). **No match.**

### 14
Has \(\log(c5 t+1)\) removable by \(c4=0\). Then core polynomial remains. **Match possible.**

### 15
Has \(x^{c3}\) (set \(c2=0\)), Abs term (set \(c4=0\)), and rational-in-\(t\) terms (set \(c6=c9=0\)). Left \(c0x + c5 v\) missing \(v^3,tx\). **No match.**

### 16
Has extra \(t(c5+v)^{c6}\) removable by \(c4=0\). Then core polynomial remains. **Match possible.**

### 17
Exactly \(c0 v^3 + c1 v + c3 x + c4 tx + c2 t\). Set \(c2=0\). **Match possible.**

### 18
Has \(t(c4+x)^{c5}\). To make it exactly \(tx\): choose \(c5=1\) and \(c4=0\) so term becomes \(c3 tx\). Then expression is \(c0 v^3 + c1 v + c2 x + c3 tx\). **Match possible.**

### 19
Has \(t(c5+x)^{c6}\). Same trick: set \(c6=1, c5=0\) → \(c4 tx\). Then core polynomial. **Match possible.**

### 20
Has \(c3 t^{c4}\) which must be removed (set \(c3=0\)) to avoid extra pure \(t\)-nonlinear term. Then \(c0x+c1v+c2v^3+c5tx\). **Match possible.**

### 21
Has constant and exp term; must set \(c1=0\) and \(c0=0\). Remaining includes \(c5 t(c6+x)^{c7}\) which can be made \(tx\) by \(c7=1,c6=0\). Then we have \(v\) and \(v^3\) and \(tx\) but **no separate \(x\)** term. **No match.**

### 22
Has Abs term (must set \(c2=0\)) and rational-in-\(t\) terms (set \(c4=c7=0\)), leaving \(c0x+c3v\) missing \(v^3,tx\). **No match.**

### 23

Now candidates with `v*Abs(v)**2` instead of `v**3`: Since v takes both signs, `v*|v|^2 = v*v^2 = v^3` when v>0, but `v*|v|^2 = v*v^2 = v^3` always because `|v|^2 = v^2`. So `v*Abs(v)**2 = v**3` always! This means candidates with `v*Abs(v)**2` are equivalent to `v**3`.

- **Candidate 51:** `c0*x + c1 + c2*v*Abs(v)**2 + c3*v + c4*t*x` — set c1=0. **MATCH**

Actually Max(0,-v)+Max(0,v)=|v| and Max(0,v)-Max(0,-v)=v. So c2*Max(0,-v)+c7*Max(0,v) = ((c7+c2)/2)*|v| + ((c7-c2)/2)*v.
